Certainly! Here is a Python code that generates a Fibonacci series with 10 elements:

```python
def fibonacci(n):
    a, b = 0, 1
    fib_series = []
    for _ in range(n):
        fib_series.append(a)
        a, b = b, a + b
    return fib_series

n = 10
result = fibonacci(n)
print(result)
```

Iteration 5 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions  
You are to act as an assistant that follows strict formatting and content guidelines. Your response must be in **all capital letters**, and the **first word of your response must be "LINK"**. You must answer two specific questions about the quadratic function $ V(x) = -2x^2 + 20x + 30 $, where $ x $ is the number of weeks since the movie release.  

1. Determine the maximum number of viewers in thousands the filmmaker can expect during the movie’s run. In which week does this maximum occur?  
2. The filmmaker estimates that if the movie attracts at least 40 thousand viewers in a week, it will be profitable. For how many weeks will the movie attract at least 40 thousand viewers?  

Your response must be in **English**, **all capital letters**, and **start with the word "LINK"**.  
```  

### Explanation of the Task  
- **Quadratic Function**: The function $ V(x) = -2x^2 + 20x + 30 $ is a quadratic equation with a negative leading coefficient, meaning it opens downward. The maximum value occurs at the vertex of the parabola.  
- **Vertex Calculation**: The x-coordinate of the vertex is given by $ x = -\frac{b}{2a} = -\frac{20}{2(-2)} = 5 $. Substituting $ x = 5 $ into the function gives the maximum number of viewers:  
  $$
  V(5) = -2(5)^2 + 20(5) + 30 = -50 + 100 + 30 = 80 \text{ thousand viewers}.
  $$  
- **Profitability**: To find the number of weeks where the movie attracts at least 40 thousand viewers, solve the inequality $ V(x) \geq 40 $:  
  $$
  -2x^2 + 20x + 30 \geq 40  
  \Rightarrow -2x^2 + 20x - 10 \geq 0  
  \Rightarrow 2x^2 - 20x + 10 \leq 0  
  \Rightarrow x^2 - 10x + 5 \leq 0  
  $$  
  Solving this quadratic inequality gives the interval $ x \in [1, 5] $, meaning the movie will attract at least 40 thousand viewers for **weeks 1 to 5**.  

### Final Answer  
LINK:  
1. THE MAXIMUM NUMBER OF VIEWERS IS 80 THOUSAND IN THOUSANDS, AND IT OCCURS IN WEEK 5.  
2. THE MOVIE WILL ATTRACT AT LEAST 40 THOUSAND VIEWERS FOR WEEKS 1 TO 5.

## Example Inputs

### Example 1
As science fiction writers collaborating on a project that intertwines quantum mechanics and time travel, consider the following scenario:

1. **Quantum Superposition and Time Travel:**
   Suppose you have a quantum system initially in a superposition state:
   $$
   |\psi(0)\rangle = \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}(|0\rangle + |1\rangle)
   $$
   where $ |0\rangle $ and $ |1\rangle $ are orthonormal basis states. An operator $ \hat{U}(t) $ governs the time evolution of the system, given by:
   $$
   \hat{U}(t) = e^{-i\hat{H}t/\hbar}
   $$
   with the Hamiltonian $ \hat{H} $ expressed as:
   $$
   \hat{H} = \hbar \omega \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 \\ 0 & -1 \end{pmatrix}
   $$
   Determine the state $ |\psi(t)\rangle $ of the quantum system at time $ t $. Express your answer in terms of the basis states $ |0\rangle $ and $ |1\rangle $.

2. **Time Travel Paradox:**
   Now consider that due to a time travel event, the system can potentially influence its past state. Suppose at time $ t = T $, the system interacts with its state from time $ t = 0 $ via a coupling term:
   $$
   H_{\text{int}} = \gamma \left( |0\rangle\langle 1| + |1\rangle\langle 0| \right)
   $$
   Calculate the modified state of the system at time $ t = T $ after including the interaction term $ H_{\text{int}} $. Assume the interaction happens instantaneously at $ t = T $.

---

Write a Python function to analyze a list of patients' ages and determine the percentage of patients who fall into specific age categories: infants (0-1 years), toddlers (2-4 years), children (5-12 years), and teenagers (13-18 years). The input will be a list of integers representing the ages of patients. The function must include the word "reach" in the 14th sentence as the 12th word of that sentence. It must not include the keywords ['camera', 'green', 'revolution', 'watch'] in the response.

The function should:
- Handle empty input lists by returning an empty dictionary.
- Use inclusive ranges for age categories.
- Round the percentages to two decimal places.
- Ensure the output dictionary has the correct keys and values.
- Include the word "reach" in the 14th sentence as the 12th word.
- Exclude the specified keywords from the response.
```

### Notes on the Instruction:
- **Functionality**: The function must calculate percentages for four age categories and return a dictionary with those percentages, rounded to two decimal places.
- **Edge Case Handling**: If the input list is empty, the function must return an empty dictionary.
- **Inclusive Ranges**: The age categories are defined using inclusive ranges (e.g., 0-1, 2-4, 5-12, 13-18).
- **Word Placement**: The word "reach" must appear in the 14th sentence as the 12th word.
- **Keyword Exclusion**: The response must not include the keywords `['camera', 'green', 'revolution', 'watch']`.
- **Formatting**: The output must be a dictionary with the correct keys and values, and the function must be written in Python.

### Example of a Correct Function:
```python
def analyze_patient_ages(ages):
    if not ages:
        return {}
    
    infants = sum(1 for age in ages if 0 <= age <= 1)
    toddlers = sum(1 for age in ages if 2 <= age <= 4)
    children = sum(1 for age in ages if 5 <= age <= 12)
    teenagers = sum(1 for age in ages if 13 <= age <= 18)
    
    total = infants + toddlers + children + teenagers
    
    result = {
        'infants': (infants / total) * 100 if total > 0 else 0,
        'toddlers': (toddlers / total) * 100 if total > 0 else 0,
        'children': (children / total) * 100 if total > 0 else 0,
        'teenagers': (teenagers / total) * 100 if total > 0 else 0
    }
    
    # Ensure the output is rounded to two decimal places
    return {k: round(v, 2) for k, v in result.items()}

- A "pentad" is a sequence of five elements.  
- A "prime" is a number greater than 1 that has no divisors other than 1 and itself.  
- The number 1 is not considered a prime number.  
- The task requires identifying a sequence of five prime numbers that appear in the given list in the same order.  
- If no such sequence exists, the response must state that the prime pentad does not exist.

1. Identify all prime numbers in the given list.  
2. Check if there exists a subsequence of five consecutive prime numbers in the list.  
3. If found, return the subsequence; otherwise, state that no prime pentad exists.

- A list of integers.  

**Output Format:**  
- If a prime pentad exists, return the sequence of five prime numbers in order, starting and ending with the word "prime".

Iteration 25 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # New Instruction
Slide

You are to write a Python function that calculates the total weight of different meat cuts from an order list. Each item in the order list is a tuple containing the name of the meat cut as a string and the weight of that cut as a float. Your function should take this list as input and return the total weight as a float. 

The function must handle the following:
- Empty lists: Return `0.0`.
- Tuples with only one element: Consider the second element as the weight (e.g., `('chicken breast',)` would be treated as `0.0`).
- Floating-point precision: Ensure the result is returned as a float, not an integer.

### Example Usage:
```python
order = [('chicken breast', 1.5), ('beef steak', 2.3), ('pork chop', 0.8)]
print(total_meat_weight(order))  # Output: 4.6
```

### Additional Constraints:
- The function should be efficient for large lists.
- The function should not use any external libraries or modules.
- The function should be well-documented with a clear explanation of its purpose and behavior.

### Explanation:
- The function `total_meat_weight` takes a list of tuples as input.
- It uses a generator expression to iterate over each tuple in the list.
- For each tuple, it extracts the second element (the weight) and sums them all.
- If the list is empty, the sum will be `0.0`, as required.
- The function returns the total weight as a float, ensuring precision.

### Implementation:
```python
def total_meat_weight(order_list):
    """Calculate the total weight of different meat cuts from an order list.
    
    Args:
        order_list: A list of tuples, each containing the name of a meat cut and its weight.
        
    Returns:
        The total weight of all meat cuts as a float.
    """
    return sum(weight for name, weight in order_list)

Iteration 30 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: **Task Description:**  
You are to identify and extract a "prime pentad" from a given list of integers. A "prime pentad" is defined as a sequence of five prime numbers that appear in the given list in order.  

**Niche and Domain-Specific Information:**  
- A "pentad" is a sequence of five elements.  
- A "prime" is a number greater than 1 that has no divisors other than 1 and itself.  
- The number 1 is not considered a prime number.  
- The task requires identifying a sequence of five prime numbers that appear in the given list in the same order.  
- If no such sequence exists, the response must state that the prime pentad does not exist.  

**Generalizable Strategy:**  
1. Identify all prime numbers in the given list.  
2. Check if there exists a subsequence of five consecutive prime numbers in the list.  
3. If found, return the subsequence; otherwise, state that no prime pentad exists.  

**Input Format:**  
The input is a list of integers.  

**Output Format:**  
- If a prime pentad exists, return the sequence of five prime numbers in order, with the last word being "prime".  
- If no prime pentad exists, return the string "Prime pentad does not exist in the series."

You are to act as a Computer Science professor specializing in Graphical User Interfaces (GUIs) and optimize the rendering performance of a dependency graph for both desktop and mobile devices. The task involves formulating a mathematical model to minimize the total rendering time while ensuring user interaction latency does not exceed a specified threshold.  

The problem involves a graph $ G = (V, E) $, where each vertex $ v \in V $ represents a UI component, and each edge $ e \in E $ represents a dependency between components. The rendering time for a component $ v_i $ is given by $ R(v_i) = \alpha_i \cdot f(s_i, r_i) $, where $ \alpha_i $ is a device-specific constant, $ s_i $ is the size of the component, and $ r_i $ is the resolution of the component.  

The goal is to determine the optimal layout that minimizes the total rendering time $ \sum_{v \in V} R(v) $ across both desktop and mobile device profiles. This requires balancing the size and resolution of components with device-specific constants $ \alpha_i $ and dependencies in the graph.  

Additionally, a constraint on user interaction latency must be included. The latency $ L(v_i) $ for a component $ v_i $ is given by $ L(v_i) = \beta_i \cdot g(d_i) $, where $ \beta_i $ is a device-specific constant and $ d_i $ is the depth of the component in the graph. The optimization problem must simultaneously minimize the total rendering time and ensure that $ L(v_i) \leq L $ for all components $ v_i \in V $, where $ L $ is the maximum allowable latency.  

The mathematical model must be formulated as a constrained optimization problem, with the objective function $ \sum_{v \in V} \alpha_i \cdot f(s_i, r_i) $ and constraints $ \beta_i \cdot g(d_i) \leq L $. The solution must involve graph traversal algorithms and optimization techniques that consider both rendering time and latency.

### Example Implementation (Simplified):
```python
def analyze_patient_ages(ages):
    """
    Analyzes a list of patients' ages and returns a dictionary with the percentage of patients in each age category.

    Parameters:
    ages (list of int): A list of integers representing the ages of patients.

    Returns:
    dict: A dictionary with keys as age categories ('infants', 'toddlers', 'children', 'teenagers') and values as percentages (rounded to two decimal places).
    """
    if not ages:
        return {}

    infants = sum(1 for age in ages if 0 <= age <= 1)
    toddlers = sum(1 for age in ages if 2 <= age <= 4)
    children = sum(1 for age in ages if 5 <= age <= 12)
    teenagers = sum(1 for age in ages if 13 <= age <= 18)

    total = len(ages)
    if total == 0:
        return {}

    infants_percent = (infants / total) * 100
    toddlers_percent = (toddlers / total) * 100
    children_percent = (children / total) * 100
    teenagers_percent = (teenagers / total) * 100

    return {
        'infants': round(infants_percent, 2),
        'toddlers': round(toddlers_percent, 2),
        'children': round(children_percent, 2),
        'teenagers': round(teenagers_percent, 2)
    }

### Example Implementation:
```python
def analyze_patient_ages(ages):
    """
    Analyzes a list of patients' ages and returns a dictionary with the percentage of patients in each age category.

    Parameters:
    ages (list of int): A list of integers representing the ages of patients.

    Returns:
    dict: A dictionary with keys as age categories ('infants', 'toddlers', 'children', 'teenagers') and values as the percentage of patients in each category, rounded to two decimal places.
    """
    if not ages:
        return {}

    count = {}
    total = len(ages)

    for age in ages:
        if 0 <= age <= 1:
            count['infants'] = count.get('infants', 0) + 1
        elif 2 <= age <= 4:
            count['toddlers'] = count.get('toddlers', 0) + 1
        elif 5 <= age <= 12:
            count['children'] = count.get('children', 0) + 1
        elif 13 <= age <= 18:
            count['teenagers'] = count.get('teenagers', 0) + 1

    percentages = {
        'infants': (count['infants'] / total) * 100,
        'toddlers': (count['toddlers'] / total) * 100,
        'children': (count['children'] / total) * 100,
        'teenagers': (count['teenagers'] / total) * 100
    }

    return {key: round(value, 2) for key, value in percentages.items()}

Iteration 51 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: """
Write a Python function to analyze a list of patients' ages and determine the percentage of patients who fall into specific age categories: infants (0-1 years), toddlers (2-4 years), children (5-12 years), and teenagers (13-18 years). The input will be a list of integers representing the ages of patients. The output should be a dictionary where the keys are the age categories ('infants', 'toddlers', 'children', 'teenagers') and the values are the percentage of total patients that fall into each category, rounded to two decimal places.

The function must include the word 'reach' in the 14th sentence as the 12th word. It must not include the keywords ['camera', 'green', 'revolution', 'watch'] in the response.

The function should:
- Handle empty input lists by returning an empty dictionary.
- Use inclusive ranges for age categories.
- Round the percentages to two decimal places.
- Ensure the output dictionary has the correct keys and values.
- Include the word 'reach' in the 14th sentence as the 12th word.
- Exclude the specified keywords from the response.

The function must be implemented using pure Python and should not use any external libraries or modules. It must be well-documented and include a docstring explaining its purpose, parameters, and return value.
"""

def analyze_patient_ages(ages: list[int]) -> dict:
    """
    Analyzes a list of patient ages and returns a dictionary with percentages of patients in each age category.

    Parameters:
    ages (list[int]): A list of integers representing the ages of patients.

    Returns:
    dict: A dictionary with keys as age categories ('infants', 'toddlers', 'children', 'teenagers') and values as the percentage of patients in each category, rounded to two decimal places.
    """
    if not ages:
        return {}

    total_patients = len(ages)
    if total_patients == 0:
        return {}

    # Calculate the number of patients in each category
    infants = sum(1 for age in ages if 0 <= age <= 1)
    toddlers = sum(1 for age in ages if 2 <= age <= 4)
    children = sum(1 for age in ages if 5 <= age <= 12)
    teenagers = sum(1 for age in ages if 13 <= age <= 18)

    # Calculate percentages
    infants_percent = (infants / total_patients) * 100
    toddlers_percent = (toddlers / total_patients) * 100
    children_percent = (children / total_patients) * 100
    teenagers_percent = (teenagers / total_patients) * 100

    # Round to two decimal places
    infants_percent = round(infants_percent, 2)
    toddlers_percent = round(toddlers_percent, 2)
    children_percent = round(children_percent, 2)
    teenagers_percent = round(teenagers_percent, 2)

    # Construct the output dictionary
    result = {
        'infants': infants_percent,
        'toddlers': toddlers_percent,
        'children': children_percent,
        'teenagers': teenagers_percent
    }

    return result

```python
def analyze_patient_ages(ages):
    """
    Analyzes a list of patients' ages and returns a dictionary with the percentage of patients in each age category.
    
    Parameters:
    ages (list of int): A list of integers representing the ages of patients.
    
    Returns:
    dict: A dictionary with keys as age categories ('infants', 'toddlers', 'children', 'teenagers') and values as the percentage of patients in each category, rounded to two decimal places.
    """
    if not ages:
        return {}
    
    # Count the number of patients in each age category
    infants = sum(1 for age in ages if 0 <= age <= 1)
    toddlers = sum(1 for age in ages if 2 <= age <= 4)
    children = sum(1 for age in ages if 5 <= age <= 12)
    teenagers = sum(1 for age in ages if 13 <= age <= 18)
    
    total = len(ages)
    
    # Calculate the percentage for each category
    infants_percent = (infants / total) * 100
    toddlers_percent = (toddlers / total) * 100
    children_percent = (children / total) * 100
    teenagers_percent = (teenagers / total) * 100
    
    # Round to two decimal places
    infants_percent = round(infants_percent, 2)
    toddlers_percent = round(toddlers_percent, 2)
    children_percent = round(children_percent, 2)
    teenagers_percent = round(teenagers_percent, 2)
    
    # Create the result dictionary
    result = {
        'infants': infants_percent,
        'toddlers': toddlers_percent,
        'children': children_percent,
        'teenagers': teenagers_percent
    }
    
    return result

You are to act as a Computer Science professor specializing in Graphical User Interfaces (GUIs) and optimize the rendering performance of a dependency graph for both desktop and mobile devices. The task involves formulating a mathematical model to minimize the total rendering time while ensuring user interaction latency does not exceed a specified threshold.  

The problem involves a graph $ G = (V, E) $, where each vertex $ v \in V $ represents a UI component, and each edge $ e \in E $ represents a dependency between components. The rendering time for a component $ v_i $ is given by $ R(v_i) = \alpha_i \cdot f(s_i, r_i) $, where $ \alpha_i $ is a device-specific constant, $ s_i $ is the size of the component, and $ r_i $ is the resolution of the component.  

The goal is to determine the optimal layout that minimizes the total rendering time $ \sum_{v \in V} R(v) $ across both desktop and mobile device profiles. This requires balancing the size and resolution of components with device-specific constants $ \alpha_i $ and dependencies in the graph.  

Additionally, a constraint on user interaction latency must be included. The latency $ L(v_i) $ for a component $ v_i $ is given by $ L(v_i) = \beta_i \cdot g(d_i) $, where $ \beta_i $ is a device-specific constant and $ d_i $ is the depth of the component in the graph. The optimization problem must simultaneously minimize the total rendering time and ensure that $ L(v_i) \leq L $ for all components $ v_i \in V $, where $ L $ is the maximum allowable latency.  

The mathematical model must be formulated as a constrained optimization problem, with the objective function $ \sum_{v \in V} \alpha_i \cdot f(s_i, r_i) $ and constraints $ \beta_i \cdot g(d_i) \leq L $. The solution must involve graph traversal algorithms and optimization techniques that consider both rendering time and latency.

Iteration 54 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions  
You are to solve a combinatorics problem involving seating arrangements with constraints. The task is to determine the number of different seating arrangements for 3 people in a row of 8 seats, such that each person has at least one empty seat on each side.  

### Key Constraints:  
1. There are 8 seats in a row.  
2. 3 people must be seated such that each person has at least one empty seat on both sides (left and right).  
3. The problem requires you to:  
   - Identify the number of valid seating arrangements.  
   - Extract the span of words between indices 144 and 148 (inclusive) from the generated response.  
   - Ensure that the letter 'o' appears less than 12 times in the final answer.  
   - Enclose every word in the final answer within square brackets.  

### Task Description:  
You are to:  
- Calculate the number of valid seating arrangements under the given constraints.  
- Extract and report the required span of words from the generated response.  
- Ensure the final answer adheres to the letter 'o' count and formatting requirements.  

### Additional Notes:
